<date>1542577971410</date><rate>4<//rate><Text>You undoubtedly will feel a sense of relief that the inside does not match the out. The construction--and the neighborhood--are unsightly.

In booking the room I noted they do not communicate as well as advertised on their website. I called and emailed to book the room and I didn't hear back for two days. I decided to book in person only to find that they had already reserved it in my name, without notifying me. In addition, the total cost was about $50 more than advertised, mainly due to the gratuity and surcharge

Whether you're to be lounging/singing with the public, or you reserve a themed room, the venue does well in bringing an extraordinary experience. That is exactly what mine and my group's takeaway was.

The group itself made up the bulk of clientele that night. I booked the Jack Daniels room, as it coalesced with the brand we work for.

Hot tip: If you are looking to get the place to yourself, consider Wednesday night.

The room capacity advertised at the front door says "25-30" people. That is a generous estimate; you'd have to be all standing shoulder-to-shoulder to fit 30. We were 17 and almost couldn't all sit comfortably.

The staff does well in explaining how to use the karaoke system. However, given we were the only ones with a booked room, the amount of service we received--minimal--did not reflect the cost.

Pro tip: If you book a room, ask for a server to bring you drinks. They charge you an 18% gratuity regardless whether you had one or not.

In fact, when you go buy your own drinks, the bartender doesn't tell you about the 18% gratuity for the room. They happily take the extra tip. The redeeming aspect of this is that they were all quite friendly. Though not 100% upfront.

I would pay that again to recreate that awesome night. I would not, however, pay the face value for the experience of booking, minimal service, and deceptive pricing.

Pro tip: Elect someone to be the screen monitor, as it takes practice to figure out the touchscreen settings and functions. The interface is archaic, but the song selection's quite modern. From Alanis Morriset, to Beyonce, they have you covered.</Text><pictures>None<//pictures>< resp>
None</resp>

<Review>I came here once with a group of friends to see what all the hype was about...

Right when you walk down the stairs from the entrance, you'll notice a bar and a nice common area with couches and a small stage for people to sing karaoke....publicly!

There are of course private rooms that you could book, but we decided it would be fun to sing in front of random strangers. Now don't get me wrong, I usually am shy about singing in front of strangers, but with a little alcohol and friends egging me on, NO PROBLEM, I'll stand up and sing in front of random strangers!

In any case, we watched several other random people sing first, and the crowd was very nice and applauded whoever went up there, even if they weren't that good. The singers ranged from younger kids to older folks (e.g. 60+) It was really an interesting experience to say the least.

Finally my friend and I requested a song from the DJ on the side and when it was our turn, we went up to sing P, Diddy's I Need a Girl. It was by far one of the funniest experiences I had in dong something spontaneous!

If you haven't been here, come check it out!

Just be wary of the surrounding neighborhood as it is located in the TL in SF.<//Review><pictures>None<//pictures>< resp>
None</resp>

<name>Elia Rho<//name>< Text>
Strongly disappointed.

As I have read articles about this place and the chef, me and my wife decided to give a shot for this Valentine's day.

The results were a nightmare.

We made a reservation and arrived on time, but the host told us that we should wait about 15 minutes. I expected any kind of apologies for this, but there were none. No comments at all.

Once we were seated, we found outdoor tables and utensils were not clean. This started to decrease the appetite and Valentine's day vibe.

Regarding the foods, we ordered aguachile and jamaica taco. Aguachile was tasty yet its plating was slightly unorganized. I started to think maybe the chef was off duty...? Anyway, aguachile was overall good.
However, jamaica taco was way too dry and mushrooms were too chewy. I guess cooking mushrooms softer and adding more sauces in it might help.

I am not a professional critic, so maybe I am not the right person to judge the foods quality, but I do not like them compared to other mexican dinings with a similar price level.

Overall, I would not recommend this place and do not think I will revisit.
I truly hope the chef here makes a hit, but it seems improvements are needed.</Text>

We waited 20 minutes just for waters let alone our drinks, and it was nearly an hour before the drinks came! This continued all night and we were left hanging outside over and over again. At one point the waitress didn't even come back at all even after we ordered a second round from her. The final straw was that when we went inside to find her, there was only one other customer in the place. We thought maybe it was busy and she was just inexperienced, but it wasn't busy so there's no possible excuse for the pathetic treatment. We were extremely patient because of the great food, but all in all we were there a total of three and a half hours and were still waiting on our second round of drinks. Again, hands down the food was amazing, but after the worst service possible it didn't really matter. I hope the owner takes it in mind to retrain or replace her/his service staff in order to make this one of the best restaurants in the area.<//Text>

<Review>We went to Vigilucci's on a Saturday night and had a party of 3. We made reservations the prior night to ensure we would get a table. Unfortunately when we got there they sat us at probably the worst table they had; right next to a parked car and in the middle of the walkway. Here are the issues I had:
(1): Seating: I would expect to be placed on the patio with a reservation. Instead we were sat a table next to the parking spots - I was less than a foot away from the front end of a car, which was a little awkward, especially when the first car left and the next car pulled in. I asked for a different table, but the hostess insisted there wasn't anything else available; I pointed out an open table on the patio, but she said that was meant for a 4 person party... however, a 3 person party was sat there less than 10 minutes later.
(2): Unsafe: Because we were next to the parking lot, and on the sidewalk, countless people "walked-through" the dining area. Most of them did not have masks. At one point the table next to us recognized a passerby and they talked for about 5 min, without masks, and about 3 feet from where we were eating. I would have expected the staff to ask these people to move on (especially since they didn't have masks on), but that never happened.
(3) Food: The food was mediocre at best. We ordered the pasta carbonara and the gnocchi. All of the dishes needed salt, the carbonara had very little pancetta, and the sauce had started to break. The gnocchi were good, however the sauce was bland. At more than $20/plate I expected far more.
(4) Ambiance: Seating issues aside, the restaurant had issues with the sound system. The music cut in and out the entire time we were there, and when it did cut in, it would blast at first, which was startling; turn OFF the music if it isn't working.

Overall, I would not recommend this restaurant. They really need to work on the seating during COVID, & the food doesn't warrant the price.<//Review><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMky6-ZpsJR-cJ6HgQ2OIUuO4ZOtmohbYVaOUsL=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMh08hx5xOyRAi4bKqkKqCWgnBrDCQX8KD1q0f8=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pictures><resp>{'time': 1599173278011, 'text': 'Our team strives to exceed expectation in all areas of our business, prioritizing reservations as we have limited seating. <user_id>103378155014543007883< /user_id>< Review>
Italian food on the decline. Used to be one of my favorite Italian restaurants. Dining partners had to send first two glasses of wine back.
I love the descriptor of the Caesar salad - "hearts of romaine with traditional dressing" . There's nothing traditional about a deconstructed salad with three slices of romaine and dressing drizzled on top. This salad, invented in Mexico, is meant to be tossed. This is the first harbinger of decline.
Next, the Calmari and rock shrimp appetizer, now features a tasteless oily batter. I actually brought the dish to the waitperson thinking there was a mistake as there was no rock shrimp present. After putting on a jeweler's loupe he was able to direct me to the miniscule pieces of rock shrimp.
Strike 2.
The Saltimbocca and pasta with oil and red pepper flakes was excellent. However, my wife's lasagna which used to be excellent was tasteless on this occasion. The waiter said he eats it every other week. That's because there's probably so much leftover they have to get rid of it.
Strike three and the decline is now complete enough to cause me to increase the Italian offerings in my own kitchen.< /Review>

<review>Meh.

EDIT: Owner graciously replied and thanked me for attending the restaurant, so I feel compelled to offer more information on my experience:

Service was top-notch and the food was prepared nicely, but I have strong opinions on Italian food.  So I'll say that my star rating was a subjective take on the flavors of the food:

I ordered the Tagliatelle alla Bolognese. Noodles were al dente.  That's good.  They were the highlight.

However, the bolognese sauce was acidic more than it was sweet and savory.  I remember watery tomato sauce, without much meat or fat.  Also, once I started eating it, I brought into question the actual combination of tagliatele with the "rag√∫"-style bolognese sauce... it was difficult to eat: the sauce was thin enough for a thinner spaghetti noodle, but didn't go well with the tagliatele, which is a no-man's land between a big flat noodle and a thin round noodle.

Maybe my mistake was ordering something I like a certain way, or maybe I'm missing what it was supposed to taste like, but an acidic bolognese sauce, to me, is off-the-mark for Italian food.

I got to taste the Gnocchi alla Sorrentina, which was also sub-standard in both texture and flavor.

Educate me if I'm off-the-mark!</review>< Pics>
None<//Pics>

< review>
Was awesome. The food was great. This is what we had:
- Caprese - this was really good and tasty, however, very steep with the price for what you get. 17+ dollars for 3 sliced tomatoes and one buffalo mozzarella ball. Should be no more than 10-13 dollars.
- spaghetti alle vongole - this was really good as well, the clams were fresh and it was nicely done.

- Eggplant Parmesan - this one was perfectly priced at 23 dollars for what you get and the food was made real well. You get a side of grilled veggies and a side of spaghetti. - the only thing with the eggplant parmesan is that it gets a little dry .. I would ask for a side pasta sauce to add to it.

Oh and we got the Chardonnay Vigilucci's which was perfect.</review>

I cannot warn you enough about The Hollywood Walk-In Clinic. First off, the reason they have such high reviews is because you get an email whether or not you were satisfied with your experience. If you are not, you leave them private feedback. If you are, you leave a review. Hence, why they have so many positive reviews.
The only reason I gave this place 1 star is because the staff at the front desk is very friendly.
The doctor I saw seems to be completely unqualified. I went in with an obvious case of pneumonia and he insisted on X-Rays and wouldn't give me the medication I needed without them. He also gave me poor suggestions when it came to healing pneumonia. I went to a second doctor the next day I was so anxious about it. He confirmed my suspicions on getting faulty recommendations. I also had to bring my medical record from the clinic for the new doctor to see and saw that he had FALSELY written that I smoke a pack of cigarettes a day (I NEVER said that!!!) and also wrote that I was not experiencing night sweats and a fever, which were two of my chief complaints!

106943268942284444359<//user_id>
<pics>None<//pics><user_name>Lawrence Miller< /user_name><Gmap_id>0x80c2bf3a4e9f65bd:0x6c7354ebde728bb<//Gmap_id>< Response>

<Date>1432876904033< /Date></record>

<UserId.>105246550807040485431</UserId.>< text>
I saught this place out because I am uninsured, and wanted a place that would top notch if I was going to have to pay. I found that! I booked an appointment the same morning.

BOOKING AN APPOINTMENT
I booked an appointment online at 9 am for 11:15 am. Only 2 hours later! There were also tons of other appointment times after that, and the next days, open. They sent me a confirmation email within 20 minutes.

PARKING
I read online that there was parking available (which, honestly was part of the reason also). There's a small parking lot attached to the clinic @Wilcox and Selma, it fits about 10-12 cars maybe. You walk straight from the parking lot into the clinic!

PROCESS
I got there at 11, parked and went straight to the front desk. She asked if it was my first time, I told her, yes, and they gave me a short 1 pager to take your information down. I went back up and handed it to her, and my ID also (which they take if you're uninsured.)
I waited maybe 10 minutes, and they called me into the office (and gave me ID back when I walked in). They took me into the exam room, asked me some questions, took my vitals, weight, etc. The whole time, they've been super nice, professional and clear/concise.

After the vitals, she took me to another room and had me wait there for the clinician. 5 minutes later, the clinician, Amanda something, came in and asked me about my reasoning for being there. She was kind, patient, and listened to all my concerns, even made me feel calm. She offered (but didn't push) x-rays. So we talked a bit more and then she said to wait for the x-ray tech.

Waited maybe 5 minutes, and he came in and took me to the x-ray room. He gave me a gown to change into, closed the curtain to give me privacy and went away. When I was done, he took the x-rays and was very clear, but light-hearted about the whole thing.

I changed back and walked myself back to the room. Within 5-10 minutes, the clinician came back and told me about my results, and offered a prescription, and told me about their 1-week free follow up. So that if things change, to come back within a week if need be. She went to get a prescription and came back swiftly with it (easy to read one-page print out I took to CVS Pharmacy with ease). She directed me to visit the front desk on my way out to pay, which I did next. The prices listed in the pamphlet are clear, and there are no hidden fees or taxes to add. I paid $159 for the visit ($89) + x-ray ($70).

I got there at 11 for an 11:15 appointment, and was out by 12p.</text>

< Text>
As other reviews have mentioned these guys are pretty seamless!

I have a weird insurance where it is both HMO and PPO, but by default it looks HMO. The receptionist at first was going to turn my insurance away, but was happy to confirm it is in fact both!

The wait was really not a big deal! 30 minutes? Maybe? Including confirming my insurance. All staff were super friendly.

The PA answered all my questions, even some embarrassing ones I had with major professionalism and no judgement!

We were going to do a blood test, but my veins weren't cooperating, you can come back within 7 days for a free check up if your symptoms of whatever ailed you are persisting. I will be returning tomorrow to try and do my blood after I drink tons of water and not be dehydrated this time. :)

They diagnosed my simple cold as well! I wanted to double check since I am prone to bronchitis and was having major chest congestion! The office is very clean, there are phone chargers, wifi, tea/water, the music is spa like music to keep you relaxed.

I will be returning. I Might use them as more of my regular doc even though my deductible is higher ($25 vs $10), but they are very convenient.  I would have walked if I wasn't feeling so icky!< /Text>

<time>1544820130964</time><rating>5< /rating>< Text>
We have been to this place on numerous occasions.  I actually prefer this place over my son's pediatrician!  LOL  We've been coming here for 2yrs now & even though there might be a wait sometimes (depending on the time of day) it's BETTER than any Dr.'s office I've been in (regarding wait time) for sure!
My son has had issues w/a possible broken/sprained ankle as well as just being very ill & each & every time the staff is professional, timely, caring & patient w/my boy.  It's one of the FEW urgent care places around that will see kids.

I've read some of the other reviews of patients not being happy b/c whatever medication didn't help & they needed to find somewhere else to go but I would LOVE to address this.  I used to work for a pharmaceutical company & we used to joke about how too many Dr.'s kill an ant w/a sledgehammer.  This place DOES NOT do that!

When you're sick, the PA or Dr. 'should' give you something appropriate & NOT the strongest antibiotic out there in order to kill off the infection.  I don't want to go into too much detail to lose people here but you don't want to give someone a Fluoroquinolone when you could take a 3rd generation Cephalosporin.

The Dr./PA is actually looking out for you!  AND this clinic will see you FREE the 2nd time for the same issue if you're not getting better after the 1st appointment within 7 days!
So that takes care of "if you didn't get better" or the medication isn't "strong enough".  ;)< /Text>

<Rate>4<//Rate><review>During my extended stay trip to L.A. I needed to get a prescription refilled, one of those that you need to see a doctor every few months in order to do so. Found Hollywood Walk-In Clinic here on Yelp and the reviews were great. Not having insurance the $79  basic office visit charge seemed very reasonable. The location is on the corner of Wilcox & Selma. The sign on the building says "Urgent Care" & there is FREE parking in a fenced lot with about a dozen tight parking spots. It's caddy-corner from the Post Office if that helps.

The waiting room: clean with large windows, ample seating (vinyl on chairs is cracking),  tea bags and water for patients although the tea bags were gone by my late afternoon visit, flat panel tv was turned on but muted & a few magazines.

The receptionist: there were 2, not overly peppy & friendly but not rude.

The wait: 50 minutes in the waiting room then I was called back by a nurse who asked a few questions, took my blood pressure & put me in a exam room where I waited another 8-ish minutes for the doctor. I was seen by a PA and yes, she was super youthful looking but my issue was simple and she did go back and consult with, I assume a certified medical doctor, before writing my prescriptions. She took the time to listen & asked the appropriate questions. I figured while I was there I'd ask for an allergy nasal spray since I was starting to have an issue with my allergies and she gave me a prescription for that too.  She sent me back out into the waiting room and within a couple of minutes I was handed my prescription, paid and was on my way.  The prescription provided 2 refills which was great since I am stuck in L.A. for an unknown length of time.

The negatives: long wait to see doctor & the 2 guys who were coughing non-stop and not covering their mouths. I'm sure if I had asked for a mask to protect myself from their spewing germs they would have provided one but I kept thinking one of us would be called back and it would be over....my mistake, but its 2 days later and so far no signs of being contaminated with the flu. I had a flu shot for the first time this year thankfully.

I'd definitely go back here if the need arises.</review>< Pics>
